      <p>
       <b>
        Houston–The Woodlands–Sugar Land
       </b>
       is the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Metropolitan_Statistical_Areas" title="List of Metropolitan Statistical Areas">
        fifth-most populous
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_statistical_area" title="Metropolitan statistical area">
        metropolitan statistical area
       </a>
       (MSA) in the United States, encompassing nine counties along the
       <a href="/wiki/Gulf_Coast_of_the_United_States" title="Gulf Coast of the United States">
        Gulf Coast
       </a>
       of the state of
       <a href="/wiki/Texas" title="Texas">
        Texas
       </a>
       . Colloquially referred to as
       <b>
        Greater Houston
       </b>
       , the 10,000-square-mile (26,000 km
       <sup>
        2
       </sup>
       ) region is centered around
       <a href="/wiki/Harris_County,_Texas" title="Harris County, Texas">
        Harris County
       </a>
       , the third-most populous county in the nation, which contains the city of
       <a href="/wiki/Houston" title="Houston">
        Houston
       </a>
       —the largest economic and cultural center of the
       <a href="/wiki/Southern_United_States" title="Southern United States">
        South
       </a>
       —with a population of 2.3 million.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-2">
         [2]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Greater Houston is part of the
       <a href="/wiki/Texas_Triangle" title="Texas Triangle">
        Texas Triangle
       </a>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Megaregion" title="Megaregion">
        megaregion
       </a>
       alongside the
       <a href="/wiki/Dallas%E2%80%93Fort_Worth_metroplex" title="Dallas–Fort Worth metroplex">
        Dallas–Fort Worth metroplex
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Greater_Austin" title="Greater Austin">
        Greater Austin
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Greater_San_Antonio" title="Greater San Antonio">
        Greater San Antonio
       </a>
       . The metropolitan area is the second-largest in Texas (after Dallas–Fort Worth) with a population of 6,490,180 as of the
       <a href="/wiki/2010_United_States_Census" title="2010 United States Census">
        2010 United States Census
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-3">
         [3]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-4">
         [4]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-www.census.gov_5-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-www.census.gov-5">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USCensus04052012_6-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-USCensus04052012-6">
         [6]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7">
        <a href="#cite_note-7">
         [7]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Houston has historically been among the fastest-growing metropolitan areas in the United States; it was the fastest-growing in absolute terms during the 2013–2014 census year, adding 156,371 people.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">
        <a href="#cite_note-8">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The area grew 25.2% between 1990 and 2000—adding more than 950,000 people—while the nation's population increased only 13.2% over the same period, and from 2000 to 2007 alone, the area added over 910,000 people.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9">
        <a href="#cite_note-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Greater_Houston_Partnership" title="Greater Houston Partnership">
        Greater Houston Partnership
       </a>
       projects the metropolitan area will add between 4.1 and 8.3 million new residents between 2010 and 2050.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">
        <a href="#cite_note-10">
         [10]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div style="clear:left; float:left; width:auto; background:none; margin-bottom:0.5em; padding:0.5em 1.4em 0.8em 0;">

      <div style="clear:both;">
      </div>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">
        Geography
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Greater_Houston&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Geography">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Houston_metro_area.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="633" data-file-width="639" height="297" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Houston_metro_area.jpg/300px-Houston_metro_area.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Houston_metro_area.jpg/450px-Houston_metro_area.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Houston_metro_area.jpg/600px-Houston_metro_area.jpg 2x" width="300"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Houston_metro_area.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         An image of the Greater Houston area taken from
         <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">
          NASA
         </a>
         's
         <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle" title="Space Shuttle">
          Space Shuttle
         </a>
         during mission STS-55 (STS055-71-43) with
         <a href="/wiki/Galveston_Bay" title="Galveston Bay">
          Galveston Bay
         </a>
         and
         <a href="/wiki/Galveston_Island" title="Galveston Island">
          Galveston Island
         </a>
         visible towards the bottom of the picture
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Houston" title="Geography of Houston">
        Geography of Houston
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       According to the
       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Census_Bureau" title="United States Census Bureau">
        United States Census Bureau
       </a>
       , the Houston–The Woodlands–Sugar Land metropolitan statistical area has a total area of 10,062 square miles (26,060 km²), of which 8,929 sq mi (23,130 km
       <sup>
        2
       </sup>
       ) is land and 1,133 sq mi (2,930 km
       <sup>
        2
       </sup>
       ) is water. The region is slightly smaller than the state of
       <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts" title="Massachusetts">
        Massachusetts
       </a>
       and slightly larger than
       <a href="/wiki/New_Jersey" title="New Jersey">
        New Jersey
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">
        <a href="#cite_note-11">
         [11]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Office_of_Management_and_Budget" title="Office of Management and Budget">
        Office of Management and Budget
       </a>
       combines the Houston–The Woodlands–Sugarland MSA with four
       <a href="/wiki/Micropolitan_statistical_area" title="Micropolitan statistical area">
        micropolitan statistical areas
       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Matagorda_County,_Texas" title="Matagorda County, Texas">
        Bay City
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Washington_County,_Texas" title="Washington County, Texas">
        Brenham
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Wharton_County,_Texas" title="Wharton County, Texas">
        El Campo
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Huntsville,_Texas" title="Huntsville, Texas">
        Huntsville
       </a>
       ) to form the
       <b>
        Houston–The Woodlands, TX Combined Statistical Area
       </b>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The metropolitan area is located in the Gulf Coastal Plains
       <a href="/wiki/Biome" title="Biome">
        biome
       </a>
       , and its vegetation is classified as temperate grassland. Much of the urbanized area was built on forested land, marshes, swamp, or
       <a href="/wiki/Prairie" title="Prairie">
        prairie
       </a>
       , remnants of which can still be seen in surrounding areas. Of particular note is the
       <a href="/wiki/Katy_Prairie_Conservancy" title="Katy Prairie Conservancy">
        Katy Prairie
       </a>
       to the west, the
       <a href="/wiki/Big_Thicket" title="Big Thicket">
        Big Thicket
       </a>
       to the northeast, and the
       <a href="/wiki/Galveston_Bay" title="Galveston Bay">
        Galveston Bay
       </a>
       ecosystem to the south. Additionally, the metropolitan region is crossed by a number of creeks and
       <a href="/wiki/Bayou" title="Bayou">
        bayous
       </a>
       which provide essential drainage during rainfall events; some of the most notable waterways include
       <a href="/wiki/Buffalo_Bayou" title="Buffalo Bayou">
        Buffalo Bayou
       </a>
       (upon which Houston was founded),
       <a href="/wiki/White_Oak_Bayou" title="White Oak Bayou">
        White Oak Bayou
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Brays_Bayou" title="Brays Bayou">
        Brays Bayou
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Spring_Creek_(Harris_County,_Texas)" title="Spring Creek (Harris County, Texas)">
        Spring Creek
       </a>
       , and the
       <a href="/wiki/San_Jacinto_River_(Texas)" title="San Jacinto River (Texas)">
        San Jacinto River
       </a>
       . The upper
       <a href="/wiki/Drainage_basin" title="Drainage basin">
        drainage basin
       </a>
       of Buffalo Bayou is impounded by two large
       <a href="/wiki/Flood_control" title="Flood control">
        flood control
       </a>
       reservoirs,
       <a href="/wiki/Barker_Reservoir" title="Barker Reservoir">
        Barker Reservoir
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Addicks_Reservoir" title="Addicks Reservoir">
        Addicks Reservoir
       </a>
       , which provide a combined 400,000
       <a href="/wiki/Acre-foot" title="Acre-foot">
        acre-feet
       </a>
       of storage during large rainfall events and cover a total land area of 26,100 acres (106 km
       <sup>
        2
       </sup>
       ).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">
        <a href="#cite_note-12">
         [12]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Greater Houston's flat topography, susceptibility to high-intensity rainfall events, high level of
       <a href="/wiki/Impervious_surface" title="Impervious surface">
        impervious surface
       </a>
       , and inadequately-sized natural drainage channels make it particularly susceptible to catastrophic flooding events.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">
        <a href="#cite_note-13">
         [13]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Geology">
        Geology
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Greater_Houston&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Geology">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Underpinning Houston's land surface are unconsolidated
       <a href="/wiki/Clay" title="Clay">
        clays
       </a>
       , clay
       <a href="/wiki/Shale" title="Shale">
        shales
       </a>
       , and poorly cemented
       <a href="/wiki/Sand" title="Sand">
        sands
       </a>
       up to several miles deep. The region's geology developed from stream deposits formed from the erosion of the
       <a href="/wiki/Rocky_Mountains" title="Rocky Mountains">
        Rocky Mountains
       </a>
       . These
       <a href="/wiki/Sediment" title="Sediment">
        sediments
       </a>
       consist of a series of sands and clays deposited on decaying organic matter that, over time, transformed into oil and natural gas. Beneath these tiers is a water-deposited layer of
       <a href="/wiki/Halite" title="Halite">
        halite
       </a>
       , a rock salt. The porous layers were compressed over time and forced upward. As it pushed upward, the salt dragged surrounding sediments into dome shapes, often trapping oil and gas that seeped from the surrounding porous sands. This thick, rich soil also provides a good environment for rice farming in suburban outskirts into which the city continues to grow near
       <a href="/wiki/Katy,_Texas" title="Katy, Texas">
        Katy
       </a>
       . Evidence of past rice farming is even still evident in developed areas as an abundance of rich, dark, loamy top soil exists.
      </p>
      <p>
       The Houston region is generally earthquake-free. While the city of Houston contains over 150 to 300
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">
        <a href="#cite_note-14">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
       active surface
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Geologic_fault" title="Geologic fault">
        faults
       </a>
       with an aggregate length of up to 310 miles (500 km),
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">
        <a href="#cite_note-15">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">
        <a href="#cite_note-16">
         [16]
        </a>
       </sup>
       the clay below the surface precludes the buildup of friction that produces ground-shaking in earthquakes. These faults generally move at a smooth rate in what is termed "fault creep".
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Weather">
        Weather
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Greater_Houston&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Weather">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Climate_of_Houston" title="Climate of Houston">
        Climate of Houston
       </a>
      </div>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="List_of_hurricanes">
        List of hurricanes
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Greater_Houston&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: List of hurricanes">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable plainlinks" role="note">
       This list is
       <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:WikiProject_Lists#Incomplete_lists" title="Wikipedia:WikiProject Lists">
        incomplete
       </a>
       ; you can help by
       <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Greater_Houston&amp;action=edit">
        expanding it
       </a>
       .
      </div>
      <p>
       A number of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tropical_storms" title="Tropical storms">
        tropical storms
       </a>
       and hurricanes have hit the area, including:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Carla" title="Hurricane Carla">
         Hurricane Carla
        </a>
        (1961)
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Alicia" title="Hurricane Alicia">
         Hurricane Alicia
        </a>
        (1983)
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Allison" title="Tropical Storm Allison">
         Tropical Storm Allison
        </a>
        (2001)
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Rita" title="Hurricane Rita">
         Hurricane Rita
        </a>
        (2005)
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Erin_(2007)" title="Tropical Storm Erin (2007)">
         Tropical Storm Erin (2007)
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Ike" title="Hurricane Ike">
         Hurricane Ike
        </a>
        (2008)
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Harvey" title="Hurricane Harvey">
         Hurricane Harvey
        </a>
        (2017)
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Components_of_the_metropolitan_area">
        Components of the metropolitan area
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Greater_Houston&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Components of the metropolitan area">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:USstcou2010_HOUSTON.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4455" data-file-width="5996" height="163" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/USstcou2010_HOUSTON.png/220px-USstcou2010_HOUSTON.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/USstcou2010_HOUSTON.png/330px-USstcou2010_HOUSTON.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/USstcou2010_HOUSTON.png/440px-USstcou2010_HOUSTON.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:USstcou2010_HOUSTON.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Location in the U.S. (red)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       As defined by the Office of Management and Budget, the metropolitan area of Houston–The Woodlands–Sugar Land encompasses nine counties in Texas. They are listed below with population figures as of the 2010 U.S. Census.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_17-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-17">
         [17]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_18-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-18">
         [18]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Harris_County,_Texas" title="Harris County, Texas">
         Harris County
        </a>
        – 4,092,459
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Fort_Bend_County,_Texas" title="Fort Bend County, Texas">
         Fort Bend County
        </a>
        – 585,375
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Montgomery_County,_Texas" title="Montgomery County, Texas">
         Montgomery County
        </a>
        – 455,746
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Brazoria_County,_Texas" title="Brazoria County, Texas">
         Brazoria County
        </a>
        – 313,166
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Galveston_County,_Texas" title="Galveston County, Texas">
         Galveston County
        </a>
        – 291,309
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Liberty_County,_Texas" title="Liberty County, Texas">
         Liberty County
        </a>
        – 75,643
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Waller_County,_Texas" title="Waller County, Texas">

        </a>

       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Chambers_County,_Texas" title="Chambers County, Texas">

       </li>
       <li>

       </li>
      </ul>
      <h3>
       <span id="Municipalities.2C_CDPs.2C_and_other_communities">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Municipalities,_CDPs,_and_other_communities">
        Municipalities, CDPs, and other communities
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Greater_Houston&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Municipalities, CDPs, and other communities">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_and_towns_in_Greater_Houston" title="List of cities and towns in Greater Houston">
        List of cities and towns in Greater Houston
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Five "principal" communities are designated within Houston–The Woodlands–Sugar Land metropolitan area. The Woodlands is a
       <a href="/wiki/Census-designated_place" title="Census-designated place">
        CDP
       </a>
       ; the rest are cities:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Houston" title="Houston">
         Houston
        </a>
        – 2,242,193
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/The_Woodlands,_Texas" title="The Woodlands, Texas">
         The Woodlands
        </a>
        - 109,679
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Sugar_Land,_Texas" title="Sugar Land, Texas">
         Sugar Land
        </a>
        – 80,704
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Baytown,_Texas" title="Baytown, Texas">
         Baytown
        </a>
        – 70,330
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Conroe,_Texas" title="Conroe, Texas">
         Conroe
        </a>
        – 71,592
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">
        Demographics
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>

        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <table class="toccolours" style="border-spacing: 1px; float: right; clear: right; margin: 0 0 1em 1em; text-align:right">

      <p>
       As of 2011 Greater Houston has four of Texas' ten wealthiest communities, which include the wealthiest community,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hunters_Creek_Village" title="Hunters Creek Village">
        Hunters Creek Village
       </a>
       , the fourth-wealthiest community,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bunker_Hill_Village" title="Bunker Hill Village">
        Bunker Hill Village
       </a>
       , the fifth-wealthiest community,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/West_University_Place" title="West University Place">
        West University Place
       </a>
       , and the sixth-wealthiest community,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Piney_Point_Village" title="Piney Point Village">
        Piney Point Village
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">
        <a href="#cite_note-19">
         [19]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">
        Economy
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Greater_Houston&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Economy">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Houston_Ship_Channel_Galena.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="999" data-file-width="1500" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Houston_Ship_Channel_Galena.jpg/220px-Houston_Ship_Channel_Galena.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Houston_Ship_Channel_Galena.jpg/330px-Houston_Ship_Channel_Galena.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Houston_Ship_Channel_Galena.jpg/440px-Houston_Ship_Channel_Galena.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Houston_Ship_Channel_Galena.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Houston_Ship_Channel" title="Houston Ship Channel">
          Houston Ship Channel
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Among the ten most populous
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_metropolitan_area" title="United States metropolitan area">
        metropolitan areas
       </a>
       in the U.S., Houston ranked first in employment growth rate and second in nominal employment growth.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">
        <a href="#cite_note-20">
         [20]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 2006, the Houston metropolitan area ranked first in Texas and third in the U.S. within the category of "Best Places for Business and Careers" by
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">
         Forbes
        </a>
       </i>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">
        <a href="#cite_note-21">
         [21]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The Houston–The Woodlands-Sugar Land MSA's
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._metropolitan_areas_by_GDP" title="List of U.S. metropolitan areas by GDP">
        gross metropolitan product (GMP)
       </a>
       in 2005 was $308.7 billion, up 5.4% from 2004 in constant dollars—slightly larger than
       <a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">
        Austria
       </a>
       's gross domestic product. By 2012, the GMP has risen to $449 billion, the fourth-largest of any metropolitan area in the United States.
       <a class="external autonumber" href="http://www.bea.gov/iTable/drilldown.cfm?reqid=70&amp;stepnum=11&amp;AreaTypeKeyGdp=5&amp;GeoFipsGdp=XX&amp;ClassKeyGdp=naics&amp;ComponentKey=200&amp;IndustryKey=1&amp;YearGdp=2012&amp;YearGdpBegin=-1&amp;YearGdpEnd=-1&amp;UnitOfMeasureKeyGdp=Levels&amp;RankKeyGdp=1&amp;Drill=1&amp;nRange=5" rel="nofollow">
        [4]
       </a>
       Only 26 nations other than the United States have a GDP exceeding Houston's GAP.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-imf2011gdp-world-eu_22-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-imf2011gdp-world-eu-22">
         [22]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Mining, which in Houston is almost entirely oil and gas exploration and production, accounts for 11% of Houston's GAP—down from 21% as recently as 1985. The reduced role of oil and gas in Houston's GAP reflects the rapid growth of other sectors—such as engineering services, health services, and
       <a href="/wiki/Manufacturing" title="Manufacturing">
        manufacturing
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-houston.org_23-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-houston.org-23">
         [23]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The area's economic activity is centered in
       <a href="/wiki/Houston" title="Houston">
        Houston
       </a>
       , the county seat of
       <a href="/wiki/Harris_County,_Texas" title="Harris County, Texas">
        Harris County
       </a>
       . Houston is second to New York City in
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Fortune_500" title="Fortune 500">
         Fortune 500
        </a>
       </i>
       headquarters. The city has attempted to build a banking industry, but the companies originally started in Houston have since merged with other companies nationwide. Banking, however, is still vital to the region.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2009)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Galveston Bay and the
       <a href="/wiki/Buffalo_Bayou" title="Buffalo Bayou">
        Buffalo Bayou
       </a>
       together form one of the most important shipping hubs in the world. The
       <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Houston" title="Port of Houston">
        Port of Houston
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Texas_City" title="Port of Texas City">
        Port of Texas City
       </a>
       , and the
       <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Galveston" title="Port of Galveston">
        Port of Galveston
       </a>
       are all major
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Seaport" title="Seaport">
        seaports
       </a>
       located in this Greater Houston area.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">
        <a href="#cite_note-24">
         [24]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The area is also one of the leading centers of the energy industry, particularly petroleum processing, and many companies have large operations in this region.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">
        <a href="#cite_note-25">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The metropolitan area also comprises the largest
       <a href="/wiki/Petrochemical" title="Petrochemical">
        petrochemical
       </a>
       manufacturing area in the world, including for
       <a href="/wiki/Synthetic_rubber" title="Synthetic rubber">
        synthetic rubber
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Insecticide" title="Insecticide">
        insecticides
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Fertilizer" title="Fertilizer">
        fertilizers
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">
        <a href="#cite_note-26">
         [26]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The area is also the world's leading center for building
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oilfield" title="Oilfield">
        oilfield
       </a>
       equipment. The region is also a major center of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Biomedical" title="Biomedical">
        biomedical
       </a>
       research, aeronautics, and high technology.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27">
        <a href="#cite_note-27">
         [27]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Much of the metro area's success as a petrochemical complex is enabled by its busy man-made ship channel, the
       <a href="/wiki/Houston_Ship_Channel" title="Houston Ship Channel">
        Houston Ship Channel
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">
        <a href="#cite_note-28">
         [28]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Because of these economic trades, many residents have moved to the Houston area from other U.S. states, as well as hundreds of countries worldwide. Unlike most places, where high fuel prices are seen as harmful to the economy, they are generally seen as beneficial for Houston, as many are employed in the energy industry.
       <a href="/wiki/Baytown,_Texas" title="Baytown, Texas">
        Baytown
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Pasadena,_Texas" title="Pasadena, Texas">
        Pasadena
       </a>
       /
       <a href="/wiki/La_Porte,_Texas" title="La Porte, Texas">
        La Porte
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Texas_City,_Texas" title="Texas City, Texas">
        Texas City
       </a>
       have some of the area's largest petroleum/petrochemical plants, though major operations can be found in Houston,
       <a href="/wiki/Anahuac,_Texas" title="Anahuac, Texas">
        Anahuac
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Clute,_Texas" title="Clute, Texas">
        Clute
       </a>
       , and other communities. Galveston has the largest cruise ship terminal in Texas (and the 12th-largest in the world). The island, as well the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Clear_Lake_Area" title="Clear Lake Area">
        Clear Lake Area
       </a>
       , are major recreation and tourism areas in the region.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">
        <a href="#cite_note-29">
         [29]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Houston is home to the
       <a href="/wiki/Texas_Medical_Center" title="Texas Medical Center">
        Texas Medical Center
       </a>
       —the largest medical center in the world.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">
        <a href="#cite_note-30">
         [30]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Galveston is home to one of only two national biocontainment laboratories in the United States.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">
        <a href="#cite_note-31">
         [31]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/University_of_Houston_System" title="University of Houston System">
        University of Houston System
       </a>
       's annual impact on the Houston-area's economy equates to that of a major corporation: $1.1 billion in new funds attracted annually to the Houston area, $3.13 billion in total economic benefit, and 24,000 local jobs generated.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Economic_Impact_32-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Economic_Impact-32">
         [32]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UH_System_Economic_Impact_33-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-UH_System_Economic_Impact-33">
         [33]
        </a>
       </sup>
       This is in addition to the 12,500 new graduates the UH System produces every year who enter the workforce in Houston and throughout Texas. These degree-holders tend to stay in Houston; after five years, 80.5% of graduates are still living and working in the region.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UH_System_Economic_Impact_33-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-UH_System_Economic_Impact-33">
         [33]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Sugar_Land,_Texas" title="Sugar Land, Texas">
        Sugar Land
       </a>
       is home to the second-largest economic activities and fifth-largest city in the metropolitan area. Sugar Land has the most important economic center in
       <a href="/wiki/Fort_Bend_County,_Texas" title="Fort Bend County, Texas">
        Fort Bend County
       </a>
       . The city holds the
       <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Sugar" title="Imperial Sugar">
        Imperial Sugar
       </a>
       (its namesake), Nalco Champion, and Western Airways headquarters. Engineering firms and other related industries have managed to take the place as an economic engine.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2009)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_companies_in_Houston" title="List of companies in Houston">
        List of companies in Houston–The Woodlands-Sugar Land MSA
       </a>
      </div>

      <h3>
       <span id="College_sports_.28Division_I.29">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="College_sports_(Division_I)">
        College sports (Division I)
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Greater_Houston&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: College sports (Division I)">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Greater Houston is home to five
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Division_I_(NCAA)" title="Division I (NCAA)">
        NCAA Division I
       </a>
       programs, with four located within Houston proper. The
       <a href="/wiki/University_of_Houston" title="University of Houston">
        University of Houston
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Rice_University" title="Rice University">
        Rice University
       </a>
       play in Division I (FBS).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-deseretnews.com_34-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-deseretnews.com-34">
         [34]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The University of Houston plays in the
       <a href="/wiki/American_Athletic_Conference" title="American Athletic Conference">
        American Athletic Conference
       </a>
       , while Rice belongs to
       <a href="/wiki/Conference_USA" title="Conference USA">
        Conference USA
       </a>
       . Both schools were once part of the
       <a href="/wiki/Southwest_Conference" title="Southwest Conference">
        Southwest Conference
       </a>
       .
       <a href="/wiki/Texas_Southern_University" title="Texas Southern University">
        Texas Southern University
       </a>
       , which is a member of the
       <a href="/wiki/Southwestern_Athletic_Conference" title="Southwestern Athletic Conference">
        Southwestern Athletic Conference
       </a>
       , plays in Division I (FCS).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-deseretnews.com_34-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-deseretnews.com-34">
         [34]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Houston_Baptist_University" title="Houston Baptist University">
        Houston Baptist University
       </a>
       currently plays in Division I (FCS), mainly in the
       <a href="/wiki/Southland_Conference" title="Southland Conference">
        Southland Conference
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">
        <a href="#cite_note-35">
         [35]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Rice and Houston Baptist are widely noted for their student-athlete graduation rates, which number at 91% for Rice (tied for highest in the nation according to a 2002
       <i>
        Sports Illustrated
       </i>
       issue on best college sports programs) and 80% for HBU.
      </p>
