      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Events">
        Events
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Greater_Houston&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Events">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Houston is or has been home to various nationally known sporting events. The most notable is the
       <a href="/wiki/Houston_Livestock_Show_and_Rodeo" title="Houston Livestock Show and Rodeo">
        Houston Livestock Show and Rodeo
       </a>
       , which is the world's largest
       <a href="/wiki/Livestock" title="Livestock">
        livestock exhibition
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Rodeo" title="Rodeo">
        rodeo
       </a>
       event. Other events of importance on greater Houston include the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shell_Houston_Open" title="Shell Houston Open">
        Shell Houston Open
       </a>
       (a
       <a href="/wiki/PGA_Tour" title="PGA Tour">
        PGA Tour
       </a>
       event), the
       <a href="/wiki/U.S._Men%27s_Clay_Court_Championships" title="U.S. Men's Clay Court Championships">
        U.S. Men's Clay Court Championships
       </a>
       (
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ATP_tour" title="ATP tour">
        ATP tour
       </a>
       ), the
       <a href="/wiki/Houston_Marathon" title="Houston Marathon">
        Houston Marathon
       </a>
       , and the
       <a href="/wiki/Texas_Bowl" title="Texas Bowl">
        Texas Bowl
       </a>
       college football bowl game. From 1959 to 1987, Houston hosted the
       <a href="/wiki/Bluebonnet_Bowl" title="Bluebonnet Bowl">
        Bluebonnet Bowl
       </a>
       . Houston has also played host to three
       <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl" title="Super Bowl">
        Super Bowls
       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_VIII" title="Super Bowl VIII">
        VIII
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_XXXVIII" title="Super Bowl XXXVIII">
        XXXVIII
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_LI" title="Super Bowl LI">
        LI
       </a>
       ), the 1968, 1986, and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2004_MLB_All-Star_Game" title="2004 MLB All-Star Game">
        2004 MLB All-Star Games
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/2017_World_Series" title="2017 World Series">
        2017 World Series
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/2005_World_Series" title="2005 World Series">
        2005 World Series
       </a>
       , and the 1989, 2006, 2013
       <a href="/wiki/NBA_All-Star_Game" title="NBA All-Star Game">
        NBA All-Star Games
       </a>
       . Houston has also played host to various high school and college sporting events, including the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Big_12_Football_Championship_Game" title="Big 12 Football Championship Game">
        Big 12 Championship Game
       </a>
       and hosted the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2011_NCAA_Men%27s_Division_I_Basketball_Tournament" title="2011 NCAA Men's Division I Basketball Tournament">
        2011 NCAA Men's Final Four
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2010_NCAA_Men%27s_Division_I_Basketball_Tournament" title="2010 NCAA Men's Division I Basketball Tournament">
        2010 NCAA Men's Regional Finals
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/2010_MLS_All-Star_Game" title="2010 MLS All-Star Game">
        2010 MLS All-Star Game
       </a>
       . Houston was also considered a candidate for the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2012_Olympic_Games" title="2012 Olympic Games">
        2012
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2016_Olympic_Games" title="2016 Olympic Games">
        2016 Olympic Games
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">
        Culture
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Greater_Houston&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Culture">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       Houston's concentration of consular offices ranks third in the nation and first in the South, with 90 countries represented.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">
        <a href="#cite_note-36">
         [36]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Houston has a sizable Hispanic community. CNN/Money and
       <i>
        Money
       </i>
       magazine have recognized cities in the Greater Houston area the past three years as part of its 100 Best Places to Live in the United States. In 2005, Sugar Land, southwest of Houston in northeast Fort Bend County, was ranked 46th in the nation, and one of only three Texas cities among the Top 100. In 2006, the magazine recognized Sugar Land again, this time as the third-best city on its list.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">
        <a href="#cite_note-37">
         [37]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Also making the 2006 list were
       <a href="/wiki/League_City,_Texas" title="League City, Texas">
        League City
       </a>
       (65th) in
       <a href="/wiki/Galveston_County,_Texas" title="Galveston County, Texas">
        northern Galveston County
       </a>
       and The Woodlands (73rd) in
       <a href="/wiki/Montgomery_County,_Texas" title="Montgomery County, Texas">
        southern Montgomery County
       </a>
       . In 2007, another Houston suburb,
       <a href="/wiki/Friendswood,_Texas" title="Friendswood, Texas">
        Friendswood
       </a>
       , made the list ranked 51st in the nation. The 2006 list only includes cities with at least 50,000 residents, and the 2007 list contains only cities with less than 50,000 residents.
      </p>
      <p>
       Greater Houston is widely noted for its ethnic diversity and strong international community. In its 2010 publication "Urban Elite",
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">
        <a href="#cite_note-38">
         [38]
        </a>
       </sup>
       A.T. Kearney added the city to their list of the 65 most important world cities and ranks Houston 35th, as "...a magnet for a diverse population and business services...". The Globalization and World Cities Study Group and Network ranks Houston as a Beta- World City, "an important world city instrumental to linking their region or state to the world economy."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">
        <a href="#cite_note-39">
         [39]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Media">
        Media
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Greater_Houston&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Media">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Melcher_Center_for_Public_Broadcasting.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1024" data-file-width="1280" height="176" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Melcher_Center_for_Public_Broadcasting.jpg/220px-Melcher_Center_for_Public_Broadcasting.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Melcher_Center_for_Public_Broadcasting.jpg/330px-Melcher_Center_for_Public_Broadcasting.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Melcher_Center_for_Public_Broadcasting.jpg/440px-Melcher_Center_for_Public_Broadcasting.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Melcher_Center_for_Public_Broadcasting.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Melcher Center for Public Broadcasting at the University of Houston
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Houston–The Woodlands–Sugar Land metropolitan area is served by a public television station and one public radio station.
       <a href="/wiki/KUHT" title="KUHT">
        KUHT
       </a>
       (HoustonPBS) is a
       <a href="/wiki/Public_Broadcast_Service" title="Public Broadcast Service">
        PBS
       </a>
       member station and is the first public television station in the United States. Houston Public Radio is listener-funded radio and comprises one
       <a href="/wiki/NPR" title="NPR">
        NPR
       </a>
       member station,
       <a href="/wiki/KUHF" title="KUHF">
        KUHF
       </a>
       (KUHF News). The
       <a href="/wiki/University_of_Houston_System" title="University of Houston System">
        University of Houston System
       </a>
       owns and holds broadcasting licenses to KUHT and KUHF. The stations broadcast from the Melcher Center for Public Broadcasting, located on the campus of the University of Houston.
      </p>
      <p>
       The Houston area is served by the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Houston_Chronicle" title="Houston Chronicle">
         Houston Chronicle
        </a>
       </i>
       , its only major daily newspaper with wide distribution. The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hearst_Corporation" title="Hearst Corporation">
        Hearst Corporation
       </a>
       , which owns and operates the
       <i>
        Houston Chronicle
       </i>
       , bought the assets of the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Houston_Post" title="Houston Post">
         Houston Post
        </a>
       </i>
       —its long-time rival and main competition—when
       <i>
        Houston Post
       </i>
       ceased operations in 1995. The
       <i>
        Houston Post
       </i>
       was owned by the family of former Lieutenant Governor
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bill_Hobby" title="Bill Hobby">
        Bill Hobby
       </a>
       of Houston. The only other major publication to serve the city is the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Houston_Press" title="Houston Press">
         Houston Press
        </a>
       </i>
       —a free
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alternative_weekly" title="Alternative weekly">
        alternative weekly
       </a>
       with a weekly readership of more than 300,000.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-About_40-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-About-40">
         [40]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Galveston_County_Daily_News" title="Galveston County Daily News">
         Galveston County Daily News
        </a>
       </i>
       , founded in 1842, is that city's primary newspaper and the oldest continuously printed newspaper in Texas.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41">
        <a href="#cite_note-41">
         [41]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It currently serves as the
       <a href="/wiki/Newspaper_of_record" title="Newspaper of record">
        newspaper of record
       </a>
       for Galveston, as well as Galveston County. Radio station
       <a href="/wiki/KGBC" title="KGBC">
        KGBC
       </a>
       , on air since 1947, has also served as a local media outlet.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">
        <a href="#cite_note-42">
         [42]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div style="clear:both;">
      </div>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Education">
        Education
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Greater_Houston&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Education">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Colleges_and_universities">
        Colleges and universities
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Greater_Houston&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Colleges and universities">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_colleges_and_universities_in_Houston" title="List of colleges and universities in Houston">
        List of colleges and universities in Houston
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ezekiel_W._Cullen_Building_(Alternate).JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2432" data-file-width="3648" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Ezekiel_W._Cullen_Building_%28Alternate%29.JPG/220px-Ezekiel_W._Cullen_Building_%28Alternate%29.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Ezekiel_W._Cullen_Building_%28Alternate%29.JPG/330px-Ezekiel_W._Cullen_Building_%28Alternate%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Ezekiel_W._Cullen_Building_%28Alternate%29.JPG/440px-Ezekiel_W._Cullen_Building_%28Alternate%29.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ezekiel_W._Cullen_Building_(Alternate).JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/University_of_Houston" title="University of Houston">
          University of Houston
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Five separate and distinct state universities are located within Houston–The Woodlands–Sugar Land metropolitan area. The University of Houston is a nationally recognized Tier One research university, and is the flagship institution of the University of Houston System.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tier_One_Research_43-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Tier_One_Research-43">
         [43]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tier_One_Research_2_44-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Tier_One_Research_2-44">
         [44]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tier_One_Research_3_45-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Tier_One_Research_3-45">
         [45]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The third-largest university in Texas, the University of Houston has nearly 43,000 students on its 667-acre campus in southeast Houston.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-State_of_the_University:_Fall_2011_46-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-State_of_the_University:_Fall_2011-46">
         [46]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/University_of_Houston%E2%80%93Clear_Lake" title="University of Houston–Clear Lake">
        University of Houston–Clear Lake
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/University_of_Houston%E2%80%93Downtown" title="University of Houston–Downtown">
        University of Houston–Downtown
       </a>
       are standalone universities; they are not branch campuses of the University of Houston. The metropolitan area is home to the two largest historically black institutions in the state:
       <a href="/wiki/Texas_Southern_University" title="Texas Southern University">
        Texas Southern University
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Prairie_View_A%26M_University" title="Prairie View A&amp;M University">
        Prairie View A&amp;M University
       </a>
       . The
       <a href="/wiki/University_of_Texas_Medical_Branch" title="University of Texas Medical Branch">
        University of Texas Medical Branch
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Texas_A%26M_University_at_Galveston" title="Texas A&amp;M University at Galveston">
        Texas A&amp;M University at Galveston
       </a>
       , a branch campus of
       <a href="/wiki/Texas_A%26M_University" title="Texas A&amp;M University">
        Texas A&amp;M University
       </a>
       , are located in Galveston.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rice_University_-_Sally_Port.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2448" data-file-width="3264" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Rice_University_-_Sally_Port.JPG/220px-Rice_University_-_Sally_Port.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Rice_University_-_Sally_Port.JPG/330px-Rice_University_-_Sally_Port.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Rice_University_-_Sally_Port.JPG/440px-Rice_University_-_Sally_Port.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rice_University_-_Sally_Port.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Rice_University" title="Rice University">
          Rice University
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Several private institutions of higher learning—ranging from liberal arts colleges to a nationally recognized Tier One research university—are located within the metropolitan area. The
       <a href="/wiki/University_of_St._Thomas_(Texas)" title="University of St. Thomas (Texas)">
        University of St. Thomas
       </a>
       is the only Catholic institution of
       <a href="/wiki/Higher_education" title="Higher education">
        higher education
       </a>
       in Houston. Houston Baptist University, located in the Sharpstown area, was founded in 1960.
       <a href="/wiki/Rice_University" title="Rice University">
        Rice University
       </a>
       is one of the leading teaching and research universities of the United States and consistently ranks among the nation's top 20 universities by
       <i>
        U.S. News &amp; World Report
       </i>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47">
        <a href="#cite_note-47">
         [47]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Three community college districts exist with campuses in and around Houston. The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Houston_Community_College_System" title="Houston Community College System">
        Houston Community College System
       </a>
       serves most of Houston. The northwestern through northeastern parts of the metropolitan area are served by various campuses of the
       <a href="/wiki/Lone_Star_College_System" title="Lone Star College System">
        Lone Star College System
       </a>
       , while the southeastern portion of the city and some surrounding areas are served by
       <a href="/wiki/San_Jacinto_College" title="San Jacinto College">
        San Jacinto College
       </a>
       . Eastern portions of the area and small sections of the city are served by
       <a href="/wiki/Lee_College" title="Lee College">
        Lee College
       </a>
       . Portions of Fort Bend County are served by
       <a href="/wiki/Wharton_County_Junior_College" title="Wharton County Junior College">
        Wharton County Junior College
       </a>
       . Portions of Galveston County are served by
       <a href="/wiki/College_of_the_Mainland" title="College of the Mainland">
        College of the Mainland
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Galveston_College" title="Galveston College">
        Galveston College
       </a>
       . Portions of Brazoria County are served by
       <a href="/wiki/Alvin_Community_College" title="Alvin Community College">
        Alvin Community College
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Brazosport_College" title="Brazosport College">
        Brazosport College
       </a>
       .
       <a href="/wiki/Blinn_College" title="Blinn College">
        Blinn College
       </a>
       serves portions of Austin County. The Houston Community College and Lone Star College systems are within the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_United_States_colleges_and_universities_by_enrollment#US_Department_of_Education_Ranking" title="List of United States colleges and universities by enrollment">
        10 largest institutions of higher learning
       </a>
       in the United States.
      </p>
      <div style="clear:both;">
      </div>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">
        Transportation
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Greater_Houston&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Transportation">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Highways">
        Highways
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Greater_Houston&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Highways">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Update" role="presentation">
       <tr>
        <td class="mbox-image">
         <div style="width:52px">
          <img alt="Ambox current red.svg" data-file-height="290" data-file-width="360" height="34" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/42px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/63px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/84px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png 2x" width="42"/>
         </div>
        </td>
        <td class="mbox-text">
         <div class="mbox-text-span">
          This article needs to be
          <b>
           updated
          </b>
          .
          <span class="hide-when-compact">
           Please update this article to reflect recent events or newly available information.
          </span>
          <small>
           <i>
            (March 2016)
           </i>
          </small>
         </div>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:RF_-_Houston_West_Loop_South.1.jpeg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2448" data-file-width="3264" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/RF_-_Houston_West_Loop_South.1.jpeg/220px-RF_-_Houston_West_Loop_South.1.jpeg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/RF_-_Houston_West_Loop_South.1.jpeg/330px-RF_-_Houston_West_Loop_South.1.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/RF_-_Houston_West_Loop_South.1.jpeg/440px-RF_-_Houston_West_Loop_South.1.jpeg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:RF_-_Houston_West_Loop_South.1.jpeg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Interstate_610_(Texas)" title="Interstate 610 (Texas)">
          Interstate 610
         </a>
         in
         <a href="/wiki/Uptown_Houston" title="Uptown Houston">
          Uptown Houston
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Houston’s freeway system includes 575.5 miles (926.2 km) of freeways and expressways in the 10-county metro area.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-houston.org_23-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-houston.org-23">
         [23]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The State of Texas plans to spend $65 billion on Houston area highways by 2025. Houston freeways are heavily traveled and often under construction to meet the demands of continuing growth.
      </p>
      <p>
       The Greater Houston area has a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spoke-hub_distribution_paradigm" title="Spoke-hub distribution paradigm">
        hub-and-spoke
       </a>
       freeway structure with multiple loops. The innermost is
       <a href="/wiki/Interstate_610_(Texas)" title="Interstate 610 (Texas)">
        Interstate 610
       </a>
       , forming a roughly 42-mile (70 km)-circumference loop around downtown. The nearly square Loop 610 is quartered into "North Loop", "South Loop", "West Loop", and "East Loop". The roads of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Beltway_8" title="Beltway 8">
        Beltway 8
       </a>
       and their freeway core, the Sam Houston Tollway, are the next loop, at a diameter around 83 miles (134 km). A proposed highway project,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/State_Highway_99_(Texas)" title="State Highway 99 (Texas)">
        State Highway 99
       </a>
       (the Grand Parkway), would form a third loop outside of Houston. Currently, a completed portion of State Highway 99 runs from
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Highway_59_(Texas)" title="U.S. Highway 59 (Texas)">
        U.S. Highway 59
       </a>
       , Near New Caney, to
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Highway_59_(Texas)" title="U.S. Highway 59 (Texas)">
        U.S. Highway 59
       </a>
       in Sugar Land, southwest of Houston, and was completed in 2016. Another segment of State Highway 99 from Interstate 10 south to Farm-to-Market Road 1405 in Chambers County was completed in 2008. The next portion to be constructed is from the current terminus at U.S. Highway 290 to U.S. Highway 59 in Montgomery County. Freeways also include the Westpark Tollway, which runs from U.S. Hwy 59 to Texas Hwy 99 and the Fort Bend Parkway, which runs from U.S. Hwy 90-A to Texas Hwy 6 in Missouri City. A new interstate,
       <a href="/wiki/Interstate_69_in_Texas" title="Interstate 69 in Texas">
        Interstate 69
       </a>
       , will start at the Mexico–US border, go through the Greater Houston area, and continue on to Michigan at the Canada–US border. All of Interstate 69 has been completed in the Greater Houston area.
      </p>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Further information:
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_Houston_highways" title="List of Houston highways">
        List of highways in Houston–The Woodlands-Sugar Land MSA
       </a>
      </div>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Mass_transit">
        Mass transit
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Greater_Houston&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Mass transit">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:METRORail_4.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2304" data-file-width="3456" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/METRORail_4.jpg/220px-METRORail_4.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/METRORail_4.jpg/330px-METRORail_4.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/METRORail_4.jpg/440px-METRORail_4.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:METRORail_4.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/METRORail" title="METRORail">
          METRORail
         </a>
         in
         <a href="/wiki/Downtown_Houston" title="Downtown Houston">
          downtown Houston
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Transit_Authority_of_Harris_County,_Texas" title="Metropolitan Transit Authority of Harris County, Texas">
        Metropolitan Transit Authority of Harris County, Texas
       </a>
       , or METRO, provides public transportation in the form of buses, trolleys, and lift vans.
      </p>
      <p>
       METRO began running light rail service (
       <a href="/wiki/METRORail" title="METRORail">
        METRORail
       </a>
       ) on January 1, 2004. Currently, the track is rather short — about 22.7 miles (20.6 km) from Northline Transit Center Station through downtown Houston to the
       <a href="/wiki/Texas_Medical_Center" title="Texas Medical Center">
        Texas Medical Center
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Reliant_Park" title="Reliant Park">
        Reliant Park
       </a>
       , and lines from downtown to the East End and the University of Houston/Lower 3rd Ward. Still, the system is traveled by about 61,000 people daily, giving it the second-highest ridership per track mile in the nation. The Uptown Light Rail Line has been converted to a BRT Line and began construction in the late 2nd quarter of 2016. The BRT Line will run between the former NW Mall (which is in the process of redevelopment) and the WestPark TC. METRO's various forms of public transportation still do not connect multiple suburbs to the inner city (defined by the 610 loop), causing Houstonians to rely on the automobile as a primary source of transportation. The problem is one due the lack of a central metropolitan area transportation authority, primarily due to a few suburban counties refusing to cooperate with METRO. For example, there are multiple coach bus services that run into downtown Houston. METRO is in the late planning stages of the US 90 Commuter line which will service the Ft Bend County and SW Harris County suburban region. Prior to the opening of METRORail, Houston was the largest large major city in the United States without a rail transit system.
      </p>
      <p>
       Following a successful
       <a href="/wiki/Referendum" title="Referendum">
        referendum
       </a>
       held locally in 2004, METRO is currently in the beginning design phases of a 10-year expansion plan to add five more sections to connect to the current rail system. An 8.3-mile (13.4-km) expansion has been approved to run the service from Uptown through Texas Southern University, ending at the University of Houston campus.
      </p>
      <p>
       Some areas in east Harris County are served by
       <a href="/wiki/Harris_County_Transit" title="Harris County Transit">
        Harris County Transit
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <div style="clear:both;">
      </div>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Airports">
        Airports
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Greater_Houston&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Airports">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/Transportation_in_Houston#Airports" title="Transportation in Houston">
        Transportation in Houston § Airports
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_airports_in_the_Greater_Houston_Area" title="List of airports in the Greater Houston Area">
        List of airports in the Greater Houston Area
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Houston's largest airport (and Texas's second-largest),
       <a href="/wiki/George_Bush_Intercontinental_Airport" title="George Bush Intercontinental Airport">
        George Bush Intercontinental Airport
       </a>
       , is located in north Houston.
      </p>
      <pre>
In 2010, <a href="/wiki/Continental_Airlines" title="Continental Airlines">Continental Airlines</a> moved its headquarters from downtown Houston to downtown Chicago. The southeast of Houston has <a href="/wiki/William_P._Hobby_Airport" title="William P. Hobby Airport">William P. Hobby Airport</a>, the second-largest commercial passenger airport. Houston's third-largest airport is <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ellington_Field" title="Ellington Field">Ellington Field</a>, which houses several <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_National_Guard" title="United States National Guard">National Guard</a> and <a href="/wiki/Air_National_Guard" title="Air National Guard">Air National Guard</a> units, as well as a <a href="/wiki/United_States_Coast_Guard" title="United States Coast Guard">United States Coast Guard</a> air station and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lyndon_B._Johnson_Space_Center" title="Lyndon B. Johnson Space Center">Lyndon B. Johnson Space Center</a>'s fleet of jets that are used to train astronauts. Sugar Land has the <a href="/wiki/Sugar_Land_Regional_Airport" title="Sugar Land Regional Airport">Sugar Land Regional Airport</a>, which is the fourth-largest airport in the metropolitan area. Both Sugar Land Regional and Ellington Field serve as reliever airports for the Houston Airport System.
</pre>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Intercity_rail">
        Intercity rail
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Greater_Houston&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Intercity rail">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Amtrak" title="Amtrak">
        Amtrak
       </a>
       provides intercity rail service to the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Houston_(Amtrak_station)" title="Houston (Amtrak station)">
        Houston
       </a>
       station.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48">
        <a href="#cite_note-48">
         [48]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Intercity_bus">
        Intercity bus
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Greater_Houston&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Intercity bus">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Greyhound_Bus_Lines" title="Greyhound Bus Lines">
        Greyhound Bus Lines
       </a>
       operates services from three bus stations in the City of Houston:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Houston Greyhound Station at 2121 South Main Street
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49">
         <a href="#cite_note-49">
          [49]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        Americanos U.S. L.L.C. (Houston Southeast) at 7218 Harrisburg Blvd.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50">
         <a href="#cite_note-50">
          [50]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        Agencia Autobuses (Houston Southwest) at 6590
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Highway_59_(Texas)" title="U.S. Highway 59 (Texas)">
         Southwest Freeway
        </a>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51">
         <a href="#cite_note-51">
          [51]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       In addition, Greyhound operates services from two stops
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52">
        <a href="#cite_note-52">
         [52]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Houston Aau
       </li>
       <li>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Houston_(Amtrak_station)" title="Houston (Amtrak station)">
         Houston
        </a>
        (
        <a href="/wiki/Amtrak" title="Amtrak">
         Amtrak
        </a>
        station)
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       Greyhound also operates services to stops within other cities in the Greater Houston area, including:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Angleton,_Texas" title="Angleton, Texas">
         Angleton
        </a>
        (at Save Step Food Mart)
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53">
         <a href="#cite_note-53">
          [53]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Baytown,_Texas" title="Baytown, Texas">
         Baytown
        </a>
        (at Baytown Travel Express)
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54">
         <a href="#cite_note-54">
          [54]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Conroe,_Texas" title="Conroe, Texas">
         Conroe
        </a>
        (at
        <a href="/wiki/Royal_Dutch_Shell" title="Royal Dutch Shell">
         Shell
        </a>
        )
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55">
         <a href="#cite_note-55">
          [55]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Katy,_Texas" title="Katy, Texas">
         Katy
        </a>
        (at Sunmart
        <a href="/wiki/Texaco" title="Texaco">
         Texaco
        </a>
        )
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56">
         <a href="#cite_note-56">
          [56]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Prairie_View,_Texas" title="Prairie View, Texas">
         Prairie View
        </a>
        (at Unco Food Store)
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57">
         <a href="#cite_note-57">
          [57]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Rosenberg,_Texas" title="Rosenberg, Texas">
         Rosenberg
        </a>
        (at Shell-
        <a href="/wiki/McDonald%27s" title="McDonald's">
         McDonald's
        </a>
        )
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58">
         <a href="#cite_note-58">
          [58]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       Three
       <a href="/wiki/Megabus_(North_America)" title="Megabus (North America)">
        Megabus
       </a>
       stations additionally serve the Houston area:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Downtown - a parking lot located at 815 Pierce St across the street from
        <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Transit_Authority_of_Harris_County" title="Metropolitan Transit Authority of Harris County">
         METRO
        </a>
        's Downtown Transit Center
       </li>
       <li>
        Northwest Houston - a Shell gas station located at 13250 FM 1960.
       </li>
       <li>
        Katy Mills Mall - at Entrance 5, 5000 Katy Mills Circle.
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">
        Politics
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Greater_Houston&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Politics">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Update" role="presentation">
       <tr>
        <td class="mbox-image">
         <div style="width:52px">
          <img alt="Ambox current red.svg" data-file-height="290" data-file-width="360" height="34" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/42px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/63px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/84px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png 2x" width="42"/>
         </div>
        </td>
        <td class="mbox-text">
         <div class="mbox-text-span">
          This article needs to be
          <b>
           updated
          </b>
          .
          <span class="hide-when-compact">
           Please update this article to reflect recent events or newly available information.
          </span>
          <small>
           <i>
            (May 2013)
           </i>
          </small>
         </div>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       Politically, the Greater Houston area has historically been divided between areas of strength of the
       <a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="Republican Party (United States)">
        Republican
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">
        Democratic
       </a>
       parties.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59">
        <a href="#cite_note-59">
         [59]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The city of Houston has historically voted Democratic except for its affluent western and west-central portions, including the
       <a href="/wiki/River_Oaks,_Houston" title="River Oaks, Houston">
        River Oaks
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Westchase,_Houston" title="Westchase, Houston">
        Westchase
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Memorial,_Houston,_Texas" title="Memorial, Houston, Texas">
        Memorial
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Uptown_Houston" title="Uptown Houston">
        Uptown
       </a>
       areas, as well as the
       <a href="/wiki/Kingwood,_Houston" title="Kingwood, Houston">
        Kingwood
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Clear_Lake_City_(Greater_Houston)" title="Clear Lake City (Greater Houston)">
        Clear Lake City
       </a>
       master-planned communities on Houston's far northeast and southeast sides, respectively. All these areas, populated mostly by wealthy WASPS, favor and are almost entirely represented both in
       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Congress" title="United States Congress">
        Congress
       </a>
       and in the
       <a href="/wiki/Texas_Legislature" title="Texas Legislature">
        Texas Legislature
       </a>
       by Republicans. Democrats' strongest areas are within Loop 610, and in the largely poor and minority northern, eastern, and southern portions of Houston. Most of these areas have sizable Hispanic populations, though some northern and southern parts of the city have mostly notable African American communities. Democrats are also stronger in the more liberal
       <a href="/wiki/Neartown_Houston" title="Neartown Houston">
        Neartown
       </a>
       area, which is home to a large artist and
       <a href="/wiki/LGBT" title="LGBT">
        LGBT
       </a>
       community, and
       <a href="/wiki/Alief,_Houston" title="Alief, Houston">
        Alief
       </a>
       , which houses a sizable Asian American population.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2012)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       In 2008, almost every county in the region voted for Republican
       <a href="/wiki/John_McCain" title="John McCain">
        John McCain
       </a>
       ; only
       <a href="/wiki/Harris_County,_Texas" title="Harris County, Texas">
        Harris County
       </a>
       was won by Democratic candidate
       <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">
        Barack Obama
       </a>
       , by a small margin (51%–49%).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60">
        <a href="#cite_note-60">
         [60]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Galveston has long been a staunch Democratic stronghold, with the most active Democratic county establishment in the state.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61">
        <a href="#cite_note-61">
         [61]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Houston's suburbs are also politically divided. Such examples:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Pasadena, which went for
        <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">
         Barack Obama
        </a>
        , is heavily Hispanic and lower-middle class on its north side, which favors Democrats, and slightly more affluent on its south side, which favors Republicans. A northwestern section of the city is represented by Democrat Ana Hernandez (District 143), while the city's central core, which contains most of its population, is represented by Republican Robert Talton (District 144). A small, largely unincorporated southeastern section of the city is represented by Republican John Davis (District 129), who also represents the
        <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">
         NASA
        </a>
        <a href="/wiki/Johnson_Space_Center" title="Johnson Space Center">
         Johnson Space Center
        </a>
        . Hernandez's district is also home to
        <a href="/wiki/Galena_Park,_Texas" title="Galena Park, Texas">
         Galena Park
        </a>
        and
        <a href="/wiki/Jacinto_City,_Texas" title="Jacinto City, Texas">
         Jacinto City
        </a>
        , which also have large Hispanic populations who favor Democrats.
        <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
         [
         <i>
          <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
           <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2012)">
            citation needed
           </span>
          </a>
         </i>
         ]
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        In Fort Bend County, southwest of Houston, Democrats are strongest in northern
        <a href="/wiki/Missouri_City,_Texas" title="Missouri City, Texas">
         Missouri City
        </a>
        and older sections of
        <a href="/wiki/Rosenberg,_Texas" title="Rosenberg, Texas">
         Rosenberg
        </a>
        , which are home to large numbers of African American and Hispanic voters, while more affluent and white areas of the county, such as Sugar Land, Katy, and
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sienna_Plantation" title="Sienna Plantation">
         Sienna Plantation
        </a>
        , are heavily Republican. These areas house sizable Asian American populations, many but not the majority are largely probusiness and favor Republicans, though a sizable community of Democratic business owners does exist among the area's Asian caucuses. In the 2008 election, John McCain won the county by 51% to 49%. Republicans control every county-wide elected office.
        <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
         [
         <i>
          <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
           <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2012)">
            citation needed
           </span>
          </a>
         </i>
         ]
        </sup>
        .
       </li>
       <li>
        Montgomery County, north of Houston, is a Republican stronghold, supported by voters in affluent communities on
        <a href="/wiki/Lake_Conroe" title="Lake Conroe">
         Lake Conroe
        </a>
        and in The Woodlands. Rural residents of the county, though primarily lower- and middle-class, tend to be very socially conservative and also have a substantial Republican following. However, the city of
        <a href="/wiki/Conroe,_Texas" title="Conroe, Texas">
         Conroe
        </a>
        proper, the county seat, tends to lean Democratic. Although The Woodlands is home to many corporate transplants from Europe, Japan, Canada, and Australia, who tend to be of a more liberal persuasion, most of these people are not U.S. citizens, thus have little impact on the voting trends of the county.
        <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
         [
         <i>
          <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
           <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2009)">
            citation needed
           </span>
          </a>
         </i>
         ]
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        The mainland areas of Galveston County, north of Galveston Island, have also become increasingly divided on political issues. Democrats have a presence in
        <a href="/wiki/La_Marque,_Texas" title="La Marque, Texas">
         La Marque
        </a>
        and
        <a href="/wiki/Texas_City,_Texas" title="Texas City, Texas">
         Texas City
        </a>
        , both of which are home to large numbers of unionized refinery workers and African Americans, a traditionally Democratic voting bloc. However, Democrats' strength in this area is increasingly being superseded by newer developments in the northern areas of the county around Friendswood and
        <a href="/wiki/League_City,_Texas" title="League City, Texas">
         League City
        </a>
        that favor Republicans.
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Brazoria_County,_Texas" title="Brazoria County, Texas">
         Brazoria County
        </a>
        , south of Houston, is heavily Republican, especially in rural areas and in central portions of the county, such as
        <a href="/wiki/Manvel,_Texas" title="Manvel, Texas">
         Manvel
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Alvin,_Texas" title="Alvin, Texas">
         Alvin
        </a>
        , and
        <a href="/wiki/Angleton,_Texas" title="Angleton, Texas">
         Angleton
        </a>
        . However, Democrats perform strongly in southern portions of the county such as
        <a href="/wiki/Lake_Jackson,_Texas" title="Lake Jackson, Texas">
         Lake Jackson
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Clute,_Texas" title="Clute, Texas">
         Clute
        </a>
        , and
        <a href="/wiki/Freeport,_Texas" title="Freeport, Texas">
         Freeport
        </a>
        due to its large Hispanic population, as well as its large base of unionized refinery workers. Additionally, the northern areas of the county around fast-growing
        <a href="/wiki/Pearland,_Texas" title="Pearland, Texas">
         Pearland
        </a>
        have recently become more moderate and even Democratic compared to the rest of the county due to its ethnic diversity, as well as large numbers of
        <a href="/wiki/Northern_United_States" title="Northern United States">
         Northern
        </a>
        and
        <a href="/wiki/West_Coast_of_the_United_States" title="West Coast of the United States">
         West Coast
        </a>
        transplants.
        <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
         [
         <i>
          <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
           <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2012)">
            citation needed
           </span>
          </a>
         </i>
         ]
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        In
        <a href="/wiki/Liberty_County,_Texas" title="Liberty County, Texas">
         Liberty County
        </a>
        , east of Houston, Republicans are represented at the state and federal levels, and the county went strongly for John McCain in 2008. However, Democrats hold a near-monopoly in county politics, though in 2006, it elected a countywide Republican (the County Treasurer position) for the first time since Reconstruction.
        <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
         [
         <i>
          <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
           <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2012)">
            citation needed
           </span>
          </a>
         </i>
         ]
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Chambers_County,_Texas" title="Chambers County, Texas">
         Chambers County
        </a>
        , between Harris and Jefferson Counties, is one of the most Republican counties in the area. According to the Office of the Secretary of State, in 2008, Republicans carried all of the candidates except for one Democratic judge, who ran unopposed. The county went 75% for John McCain over Barack Obama. The same held true in 2010, when Republicans won all county-wide elections ranging from 71% to 91%.
        <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
         [
         <i>
          <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
           <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2012)">
            citation needed
           </span>
          </a>
         </i>
         ]
        </sup>
       </li>
      </ul>

      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Texas_Legislature">
        Texas Legislature
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Greater_Houston&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Texas Legislature">

      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Texas_Senate">
        Texas Senate
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Greater_Houston&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Texas Senate">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
